    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer8158093008518940185">When two teenagers steal a purse from a stroller, it results in an infant’s death.   <span id="freeText8158093008518940185" style="display:none">When two teenagers steal a purse from a stroller, it results in an infant’s death. Unaware of the enormity of their crime, Zipp and Andreas are intent on committing another. They follow an elderly woman home, and Andreas enters her house with his switchblade. In the dark, Zipp waits for his friend to come out. <br /><br />Inspector Konrad Sejer and his colleague Jacob Skarre see no connection between the infant’s death and the reported disappearance of a local delinquent. And so while the confusion outside mounts, the heart-stopping truth unfolds inside the old woman’s home. <br /><br />Unflappable as ever, Sejer digs below the surface of small- town tranquility in an effort to understand how and why violence destroys everyday lives.</span>

<div id="review_33722370" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33722370" />
    <a title="Annabelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/692710-annabelle"><img alt="Annabelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203132694p2/692710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33722370?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annabelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annabelle" href="/user/show/692710-annabelle">Annabelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33722370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4558702219451064459">This is a Norwegian mystery with that particular existential, fatalist almost nihilist point of view. And also it is postmodern in that the detective doesn’t solve anything, although his circling the perpetuators of the crime helps bring resolution, which is karmic and not from the long arm of the law. I actually liked that part. The only sane people are Inspector Sejer, his sidekick, Skarre, Sejer’s huge dog and Sejer’s girlfriend. Sejer seems the persona of a stable Europe that is struck by th</span>
  <span id="freeText4558702219451064459" style="display:none">This is a Norwegian mystery with that particular existential, fatalist almost nihilist point of view. And also it is postmodern in that the detective doesn’t solve anything, although his circling the perpetuators of the crime helps bring resolution, which is karmic and not from the long arm of the law. I actually liked that part. The only sane people are Inspector Sejer, his sidekick, Skarre, Sejer’s huge dog and Sejer’s girlfriend. Sejer seems the persona of a stable Europe that is struck by the erosion of societal structures, his girlfriend has phone sex when he is not in the mood, his side kick wears an earring. He sees young adult men with no purpose, with mindless jobs or no jobs, drinking and easily almost naturally falling into violence against others, although there is mortification after the fact. They psychodynamic motivation of the childhood of the crazy killer, and the repressed homosexuality of another character without morals, is a bit simplistic and overdrawn. However the peak of town life in Norway is wonderful, and it is psychological evocative, but all in all a bit disturbing view of humans. Except the Inspector continues and finds some small joys in life, maybe he is who we are to identify with amidst lost people and meaningless violence around us. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4558702219451064459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2009836179" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2009836179" />
    <a title="David R. Dowdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62437869-david-r-dowdy"><img alt="David R. Dowdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591273899p2/62437869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2009836179?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David R. Dowdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David R. Dowdy" href="/user/show/62437869-david-r-dowdy">David R. Dowdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62437869-david-r-dowdy?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2009836179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10686495964068881929">I was totally surprised When the Devil Holds the Candle didn’t flow like Don’t Look Back, an Inspector Sejer police procedural, an investigation in progress. Fossum changed up and wrote a thriller in progress. And I’m glad she did, because sequels can become too predictable.<br/><br/>Fossum definitely knows twisted evil. I don’t mean she’s twisted or has first-hand experience in evil (does she?). What I mean is that she developed evil characters and, in a twist, put them at odds with each other.<br/><br/>Though we </span>
  <span id="freeText10686495964068881929" style="display:none">I was totally surprised When the Devil Holds the Candle didn’t flow like Don’t Look Back, an Inspector Sejer police procedural, an investigation in progress. Fossum changed up and wrote a thriller in progress. And I’m glad she did, because sequels can become too predictable.<br /><br />Fossum definitely knows twisted evil. I don’t mean she’s twisted or has first-hand experience in evil (does she?). What I mean is that she developed evil characters and, in a twist, put them at odds with each other.<br /><br />Though we all know evil people, we often don’t know what made them that way. But, we have ideas. Brash alphas are often evil because they misuse their strengths. Meek people take all the shit the world shovels at them then suddenly crack. <br /><br />It’s interesting that Fossum took those two types, characterized them evilly, and threw them at each other. Evil can beat evil just like good can overcome evil. When the former happens, the result is uglier than evil squared. It’s terrifying and Fossum couldn’t have written a better example.<br /><br />Fossum creeps out and tosses a bit of cheese your way. You get the cheese and scamper back. Next, she doles out a bit more, but farther away so that you have to leave the cozy security of your nest. More cheese, further and further away. Again and again until you look up and she’s standing there crookedly smiling at you with her arms folded. You want to run except that your tiny pink feet are locked in the sticky trap!<br /><br />Our Inspector Sejer doesn’t play a major role until it’s too late. Even so, he’s not the same Sejer as he was in DLB. He’s as astute in his patient, plodding way, there’s no doubt. He seems younger and livelier now that Sara is more in his life and bed. Skarre is there throughout and he’s learning to become a good investigator as well.<br /><br />Interestingly, the voices are written in first person and third. That gives this well-written story a thrilling perspective. The plot, part of which might have been controversial when first published, produces a great beat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10686495964068881929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2374816980" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2374816980" />
    <a title="Angel 一匹狼" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25600796-angel"><img alt="Angel 一匹狼" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438533669p2/25600796.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2374816980?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angel 一匹狼" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angel 一匹狼" href="/user/show/25600796-angel">Angel 一匹狼</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781843430919" href="/book/show/280355.When_the_Devil_Holds_the_Candle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2374816980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17699289031713344476">A couple of teenage friends, Andreas and Zipp, are bored, without much to do. They go around bullying immigrants, stealing purses from women going on a stroll with their babies and breaking and entering in old ladies' houses. One of the last goes wrong and silly things start to happen. All the while the police and its detectives do nothing.<br/><br/>That is basically the plot of lame and silly "When the Devil Holds the Candle" a novel just because the cover says it is a novel. It is 230-pages-long of stup</span>
  <span id="freeText17699289031713344476" style="display:none">A couple of teenage friends, Andreas and Zipp, are bored, without much to do. They go around bullying immigrants, stealing purses from women going on a stroll with their babies and breaking and entering in old ladies' houses. One of the last goes wrong and silly things start to happen. All the while the police and its detectives do nothing.<br /><br />That is basically the plot of lame and silly "When the Devil Holds the Candle" a novel just because the cover says it is a novel. It is 230-pages-long of stupid plot and character decision after stupid plot and character decision. None of the motives of the characters make much sense, and even if Karin Fossum tries to infuse them with lives and motives and justify bad decisions, it all ends up being risible, laughable, a bad joke. Even if the book is short, it could actually have been one forth, because there is so much padding and stretching without end that it makes things crawl to a stop.<br /><br />This is no crime/mystery novel. This is just a sad excuse of a book.<br /><br />The best: how the author tries to make the characters human<br /><br />The worst: everything else: it's a mess, the character's decisions make no sense, the plot is silly and worth of a rubbish bin, there is no mystery, there is no point to the whole proceedings<br /><br />Other options: any other mystery novel; if you want one with actual character development you can have Agatha Christie and Miss Marple; if you want them from the cold, you can pick from Camilla Läckberg to Henning Mankell; you can go Japanese and pick Miyabe Miyuki or Natsuo Kirino... Anything else but this.<br /><br />1/10<br /><br />(English translation by Felicity David)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_207558129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207558129" />
    <a title="Edmund Leow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5831963-edmund-leow"><img alt="Edmund Leow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311130205p2/5831963.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/207558129?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edmund Leow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edmund Leow" href="/user/show/5831963-edmund-leow">Edmund Leow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207558129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3743779657799593620">The story is chilling because the characters are so believeable. It's not about a murderer with some strange fixation or obsession, no revenge that dates 40 years ago, or a murderer who derives joy from killing. It's not about who did it, but how did things end up like this? It is about how everyday people's lives can quickly spiral out of control, or descend to tragedy - through pure chance and even though inaction... It is about how close to the edge most of us are, without realising. It makes</span>
  <span id="freeText3743779657799593620" style="display:none">The story is chilling because the characters are so believeable. It's not about a murderer with some strange fixation or obsession, no revenge that dates 40 years ago, or a murderer who derives joy from killing. It's not about who did it, but how did things end up like this? It is about how everyday people's lives can quickly spiral out of control, or descend to tragedy - through pure chance and even though inaction... It is about how close to the edge most of us are, without realising. It makes you feel that this could happen to anyone.. how we could end up being a killer, or a victim... or both, at the same time. It makes you question the sanity of everyone around you, and even yourself...<br /></span>

<div id="review_290267066" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/290267066" />
    <a title="Bill Garrison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/977395-bill-garrison"><img alt="Bill Garrison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442975380p2/977395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/290267066?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill Garrison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill Garrison" href="/user/show/977395-bill-garrison">Bill Garrison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290267066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3698403524116105060">Norwegian author Karen Fossum's WHEN THE DEVIL HOLDS THE CANDLE is another excellent entry into the Inspector Konrad Sejer series. I've read over half of the books in the series, and while they are very readable and offer fascinating looks into the minds of the deluded, criminal, and insane, they really don't feature the standard format of the cops looking for clues and catching the bad guys.<br/><br/>In this novel, Fossum looks at what happens when people considered normal give into evil, or evil overcom</span>
  <span id="freeText3698403524116105060" style="display:none">Norwegian author Karen Fossum's WHEN THE DEVIL HOLDS THE CANDLE is another excellent entry into the Inspector Konrad Sejer series. I've read over half of the books in the series, and while they are very readable and offer fascinating looks into the minds of the deluded, criminal, and insane, they really don't feature the standard format of the cops looking for clues and catching the bad guys.<br /><br />In this novel, Fossum looks at what happens when people considered normal give into evil, or evil overcomes them, and they committ horrendous crimes that they wouldn't normally consider. Most of the book follows Zipp and Andreas, two teenagers that wander around aimlessly drinking beer, looking at girls, and watching "Blade Runner" at Zipp's house. The boys occasionally rob women of their handbags for beer money. On one horrible day, they rob a woman pushing a stroller and set in motion a tragic train of events that lead to one boy missing, and one boy refusing to tell the police what he knows.<br /><br />Conrad Sejer, and his younger partner Jacob Skarr, work on the periphery of the investigation. They at first dismiss Andreas's mother's claim that her boy is missing. After all, boys will be boys. But soon they suspect something is wrong. They are basically right in the middle of everything, but the novel ultimately shifts back to Zipp and Andreas. This novel is about them and what happens to a person when the Devil holds the candle.<br /><br />While the lack of action by Sejer and Skarre is disappointing, it doesn't take away from how much I enjoyed the novel. Fossum's novels are different, and she's a best seller in Norway, so I love exploring novels from other countries.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3698403524116105060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9175589831932483912" style="display:none">It's hard to like a book this horrifying. It examines the intersection of casual petty crimes committed by bored, drunken young men with unintended, life-shattering consequences for them and their victims. As it is ofen said, "things get out of hand." <br /><br />If the story had stuck to that it wouldn't have been so devastating a story, but complicating all the stories is the failure to help when it is critically needed. Teens who don't help themselves or each other when their lives depend on it. Adults, even close family friends, who knowingly watch extreme suffering of beautiful young people and don't say a thing; breaking under a lifetime of their own personal weakness and failure to act on their own behalf. <br /><br />It's a contrast between people who break but live on, and young people in the process of breaking as they are faced with a vague adulthood.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_308928873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308928873" />
    <a title="Mary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5500603-mary"><img alt="Mary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567777318p2/5500603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308928873?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary" href="/user/show/5500603-mary">Mary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308928873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8523699258212716698">A little different from her previous two books, featuring Sejer and Skarre, but equally as good. This one is about two 18-year old friends, Andreas and Zip, bored, broke and about to cross the line in a series of events that will leave several lives changed forever. Zip is led by Andreas into a purse snatching incident, involving a mother and her 4-month old baby, when Andreas takes the womans purse, she gives chase and does not secure the brake on the pram. The pram topples over a ledge at the </span>
  <span id="freeText8523699258212716698" style="display:none">A little different from her previous two books, featuring Sejer and Skarre, but equally as good. This one is about two 18-year old friends, Andreas and Zip, bored, broke and about to cross the line in a series of events that will leave several lives changed forever. Zip is led by Andreas into a purse snatching incident, involving a mother and her 4-month old baby, when Andreas takes the womans purse, she gives chase and does not secure the brake on the pram. The pram topples over a ledge at the seafront and the baby falls out. Although Zip tries to stop the pram from falling over, he does not reach it on time and is left shaken and horrified by what has happened. Andreas is also feeling guilty and so they then go on a drinking session to try and forget what happened. Later that night, Andreas follows and elderly woman home, with the intention of mugging her, having clearly not learned his lesson. He leaves Zip outside the house, goes in and is never seen again. It is a well told story, some parts in the words of the woman Andreas has followed to her home and this part makes for a very interesting perspective of the plot. It is distressing, without being graphic and gives the reader an insight into why people take certain decisions, which can only lead to disastrous consequences. There is a little touch of the Stephen Kings in this book, which provides us with some chilling moments, but yet it is written in a way that we can sympathize with the characters central to the plot at the same time. I would definitely recommend this series as a must for crime/mystery fans.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8523699258212716698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3851557721241635511" style="display:none">I normally give Karin Fossum's Inspector Sejer 5 stars, as they are so well crafted. This one is equally well-crafted but is amazingly depressing. [Guess I am a wimp :) ]<br /><br />First paragraphs<br />Chapter 1 The courthouse. September 4, 4 P.M. Jacob Skarre glanced at his watch. His shift was over. He slipped a book out of his jacket pocket and read the poem on the first page. It's like virtual reality, he thought. Poof!—and you're in a completely different landscape. The door to the corridor stood open, and suddenly he was aware that someone was watching him, someone just beyond the range of his excellent peripheral vision. A vibration, light as a feather, barely perceptible, finally reached him. He closed the book. "Can I help you?" The woman didn't move, just stood there staring at him with an odd expression. Skarre looked at her tense face and thought she seemed familiar. She was no longer young, maybe about sixty, and wore a coat and dark boots. There was a scarf around her neck, just visible; he could see it above her collar. Its pattern offered a sharp contrast to what she most likely possessed in the way of speed and elegance: racehorses with jockeys in colorful silks against a dark blue background. She had a wide, heavy face, elongated by a prominent chin. Her eyebrows were dark and had grown almost together. She was clutching a handbag against her stomach.<br /><br />Fossum, Karin (2007-06-04). When the Devil Holds the Candle (Inspector Sejer Mysteries) (pp. 1-2). Houghton Mifflin Harcourt. <div id="review_8620476" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8620476" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/225991-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1185743262p2/225991.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8620476?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/225991-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8620476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9717891296044386880">I struggled a bit getting into this unconventional mystery novel, which doesn't really, in my mind, have any of the qualities that are typically associated with mysteries aside from the fact that there's a crime involved. One thing that I had to adjust to was the fact that the very interesting and likable Inspector Konrad Sejer is essentially a supporting character here, and I went in hoping to spend more time with him than the book provided. That's not to say that the characters we do spend mos</span>
  <span id="freeText9717891296044386880" style="display:none">I struggled a bit getting into this unconventional mystery novel, which doesn't really, in my mind, have any of the qualities that are typically associated with mysteries aside from the fact that there's a crime involved. One thing that I had to adjust to was the fact that the very interesting and likable Inspector Konrad Sejer is essentially a supporting character here, and I went in hoping to spend more time with him than the book provided. That's not to say that the characters we do spend most of our time with aren't interesting, because they are. There's Andreas, a beautiful and troubled 18-year-old who is obsessed with Blade Runner, and as a fan of the film myself I enjoyed the way that Fossum would occasionally work quotes from the movie into this book. And there's Irma, an older woman whose voice we hear in first-person, and not unlike the narrator of Edgar Allan Poe's "The Tell-Tale Heart," Irma's attempts to convince us of her sanity only show us how disturbed she is. Despite her actions, I found her a somewhat sympathetic character--after all, she did not choose to be mentally ill. And I like the way that her sense of isolation has a kind of counterpoint in Sejer's life, as he struggles to feel connected to a new girlfriend who is very different from himself. I felt that there were a few unlikely coincidences, and some frustratingly shoddy police work, but thanks to the psychologically complex and compelling characters I still enjoyed this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9717891296044386880" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer595988964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14278215524926264476">This book is purely genial. I don't think I have ever "encountered" such a improbable and sadly deranged "villain".<br/>I am using brackets when I say villain because there is no black and white in this book, everything is grey, from atmosphere to characters.<br/>We really get to like the two weird but not bad hearted loner sort of teens despite their somewhat hasty and unthoughtful actions we might condone, all of this is just an intro into the black void which will swallow Andreas halfway through the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText14278215524926264476" style="display:none">This book is purely genial. I don't think I have ever "encountered" such a improbable and sadly deranged "villain".<br />I am using brackets when I say villain because there is no black and white in this book, everything is grey, from atmosphere to characters.<br />We really get to like the two weird but not bad hearted loner sort of teens despite their somewhat hasty and unthoughtful actions we might condone, all of this is just an intro into the black void which will swallow Andreas halfway through the book, literally.<br />As with many other books, this was a pure chance which opened doors / trapdoors? to something sinister, malicious and indescribable, an eclipse of human nature.<br />This is a dark psychological masterpiece, depressing and shattering. Again not for those who prefer action packed novels or whodunnits.<br />I think I will be reading more of this one, it's hard to forget even details like the shopping list.<br />I would have deducted half a star only because I am really unsure what might have happened to the second youth and because I am not sure I understood completely why Irma's husband met his fate the way he did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14278215524926264476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_136142331" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136142331" />
    <a title="Nick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1868162-nick"><img alt="Nick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231185226p2/1868162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136142331?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick" href="/user/show/1868162-nick">Nick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1868162-nick?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1868162-nick?shelf=translated">translated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136142331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3009631026784606306">This is an odd book, not attributable entirely to a translation from Norwegian, I would imagine. As my obsession for Scandinavian mysteries moved from Sweden to Norway last year, I thought I should check out Fossum, who is listed by other obsessives as a must-read author in the sub-genre. There's a dream-like quality to the prose generated by the narrator, an aging and bitter woman who is both victim and perpetrator that reminds me of certain short stories and less-famous novels by Patricia High</span>
  <span id="freeText3009631026784606306" style="display:none">This is an odd book, not attributable entirely to a translation from Norwegian, I would imagine. As my obsession for Scandinavian mysteries moved from Sweden to Norway last year, I thought I should check out Fossum, who is listed by other obsessives as a must-read author in the sub-genre. There's a dream-like quality to the prose generated by the narrator, an aging and bitter woman who is both victim and perpetrator that reminds me of certain short stories and less-famous novels by Patricia Highsmith. We're meant, I think, to have ambivalent feelings about her, indeed, about all of the characters except the police, who are almost in the background, despite the fact that this is nominally a police procedural. We enter the story late in the game and go back and forth in time until catching up to the horrible situation, which is some ways more of a moral tale than a mystery. Until the very end, when the twist is revealed. Liked, not loved it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3009631026784606306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5765992364817758385">This is the second book I’ve read of Fossum’s Norwegian mysteries. If these two are typical, her work tends more to psychological studies than traditional who-dun-its. Fossum’s insights can be penetrating as in this example of Inspector Sejer on the death of his aged mother who had been comatose for years—“Mother—he murmured. How strange to say that word out loud and never to hear an answer again. He sank back in the chair, thinking that he ought to go home. He stood up, but left the chair where</span>
  <span id="freeText5765992364817758385" style="display:none">This is the second book I’ve read of Fossum’s Norwegian mysteries. If these two are typical, her work tends more to psychological studies than traditional who-dun-its. Fossum’s insights can be penetrating as in this example of Inspector Sejer on the death of his aged mother who had been comatose for years—“Mother—he murmured. How strange to say that word out loud and never to hear an answer again. He sank back in the chair, thinking that he ought to go home. He stood up, but left the chair where it was as if it might yet keep her company. He happened to look at his watch again. It was 12:52. He did the arithmetic in his mind. Seven minutes. That’s how much time he had granted her, to thank her for everything. Seven minutes to say thank you for a whole lifetime. Take all the time you need.<br />He started shaking. His shoulders hunched in shame. He turned around and went back to the bed, sat on the edge, picked up her gaunt hands and held them tight. For a long time.” <br /></span>

I am going to give Fossum the benefit of the doubt and ASSUME that the terrible convoluted story line was due to massive editing errors. Literally from one sentence to the next paragraph, with no ellipses in between to alert you to a change in character, there would be a "new voice" a new point of view with NO IDEA who was "speaking." This happened so many times and it WAS SO DAMN CONFUSING!! One moment you're in Zipp's head and the next you think he is bein</span>
  <span id="freeText5478009691165551248" style="display:none">I did not finish this mess of a book. I am going to give Fossum the benefit of the doubt and ASSUME that the terrible convoluted story line was due to massive editing errors. Literally from one sentence to the next paragraph, with no ellipses in between to alert you to a change in character, there would be a "new voice" a new point of view with NO IDEA who was "speaking." This happened so many times and it WAS SO DAMN CONFUSING!! One moment you're in Zipp's head and the next you think he is being described as a girl (when actually it's another character) because there is NO BREAK in the page!!! Frustrating as hell. The mother with the baby? Again, the transition back to her is done in the same way. I got a headache and although I was sort of curious as to how Andreas finally meets his end I was not curious enough to continue reading when there are so many other books out there to be read!!!</span>

<div id="review_372084665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/372084665" />
    <a title="Doug Baird" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7528063-doug-baird"><img alt="Doug Baird" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341948481p2/7528063.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/372084665?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doug Baird" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doug Baird" href="/user/show/7528063-doug-baird">Doug Baird</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer372084665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2561720888730130385">My first Fossum book, so it's hard to draw any conclusions, but I was struck by the difference in emphasis on the part of the cops. In most US crime novels and police procedurals the cops are tough guys, macho men, avenger types. Criminals don't just do evil deeds, they are evil men, or women. <br/>Fossum's cops are just as efficient at solving crimes, which in some instances is not very efficient, but their attitudes are much less anger/vengence-laced. The criminals are not inherently evil, they're </span>
  <span id="freeText2561720888730130385" style="display:none">My first Fossum book, so it's hard to draw any conclusions, but I was struck by the difference in emphasis on the part of the cops. In most US crime novels and police procedurals the cops are tough guys, macho men, avenger types. Criminals don't just do evil deeds, they are evil men, or women. <br />Fossum's cops are just as efficient at solving crimes, which in some instances is not very efficient, but their attitudes are much less anger/vengence-laced. The criminals are not inherently evil, they're mentally disturbed. When apprehended, they're treated with more dignity than I'm used to seeing in the USA. I'm not suggesting that this is a good thing or a bad thing - it's just interesting to take note of. I'm sure I'm not the first person to notice this difference in tone, and I would be interested to hear the perspective of others.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2561720888730130385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sandi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1185451-sandi"><img alt="Sandi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1248800038p2/1185451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1429904944?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandi" href="/user/show/1185451-sandi">Sandi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer16413838740493952317">While part of the Inspector Sejer series, Sejer and the police actually have a small role in the narrative. Instead this was more psychological suspense with an emphasis on characterizations. Dark, suspenseful, and, though very well written, quite disturbing. </span>

<div id="review_2320474469" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2320474469" />
    <a title="Lukasz Pruski" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2989615-lukasz-pruski"><img alt="Lukasz Pruski" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362764033p2/2989615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320474469?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lukasz Pruski" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lukasz Pruski" href="/user/show/2989615-lukasz-pruski">Lukasz Pruski</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320474469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8755872281110047016">"<i>He slipped his arm around her waist and held on tight, lifting her from the chair. She squealed with glee, but he noted with satisfaction the tiny hint of panic as he carried her across the room.</i>"<br/><br/>Karin Fossum, one of my most favorite writers manages to surprise me in three different ways with her <i>When the Devil Holds the Candle</i> (1998). First of all, I am surprised that this is again not a great book, not even - I am afraid - a very good one. It is far below the level of Ms. Fossum's best work l</span>
  <span id="freeText8755872281110047016" style="display:none">"<i>He slipped his arm around her waist and held on tight, lifting her from the chair. She squealed with glee, but he noted with satisfaction the tiny hint of panic as he carried her across the room.</i>"<br /><br />Karin Fossum, one of my most favorite writers manages to surprise me in three different ways with her <i>When the Devil Holds the Candle</i> (1998). First of all, I am surprised that this is again not a great book, not even - I am afraid - a very good one. It is far below the level of Ms. Fossum's best work like her masterpiece <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1170019235" rel="nofollow noopener"> <i>Black Seconds</i> </a> and below the beautifully sad <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2089939914" rel="nofollow noopener"> <i>Indian Bride</i> </a>. <br /><br />Further, the novel has surprised me in that I like the thread about Chief Inspector Sejer's personal life. I have never warmed to his persona, seemingly aloof and cold, but here the author humanizes the detective through the presence of his girlfriend. Also, the whole thread is quite well written: many scenes between Sejer and Sara ring true. Ms. Fossum does a great job writing about love between mature people - not an easy thing to do. One can even find a short passage that is quite erotically charged - I have never seen it before in the author's works even if I have read almost all her novels that have been translated into English.<br /><br />Alas, the last surprise is again of an unpleasant kind. The partial solution of the mystery thread is based on a rather cheap literary device, used and abused by many authors before, authors not as talented as Ms. Fossum. The mystery thread also greatly stretches the bounds of plausibility but then one does not read this author's books for the mystery component but rather for the characters' psychology.<br /><br />The mystery thread is based on the disappearance of a young man. An elderly woman accosts Sejer's assistant, Skarre, during his appearance in court. The woman - who cryptically tells Skarre that the missing person does not have long to live - seems confused and the detective even suspects mental illness. The rest of the novel alternates between four threads: an internal monologue of one of the central characters, a thread that focuses on adventures, some of criminal nature, of two young men, Andreas and Zipp. The third thread, a procedural one, follows the investigation, and the last one is the "love story" of Sejer and Sara. While the chronological order of events is not kept strict the author manages to build mystery and suspense.<br /><br />Other than the sweet and well-written passages about the Sejer-Sara relationship the best thing in the novel is the character of Andreas. I find him a full-bodied person rather than a paper-thin template. Andreas "saunters through life" (a great phrase!) with no ambition, no interests, no enthusiasm for anything. As many other characters in the novel he carries a secret, which distorts his life.<br /><br />I very much like the slight ambiguity of the ending since it validates my belief that no one ever knows what really is going on around them. A good, readable, engrossing novel, just not an extraordinary one.<br /><br />Three and a quarter stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8755872281110047016" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L" href="/user/show/1156396-l">L</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2663091992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18037308983967450238">This is a strange one, for me. First, it's very interior, which I generally don't like in a mystery. Except this time I couldn't put it down. Second, it's creepy, very creepy. And yet, I couldn't put it down.<br/><br/>You know from the book description that two teens, Zipp--unemployed, not terribly bright, but sort of decent--and Andreas--attractive & charming, with an expectation that things will go his way--who are going not much of any where in life, liven up their evening by steeling a woman's handbag</span>
  <span id="freeText18037308983967450238" style="display:none">This is a strange one, for me. First, it's very interior, which I generally don't like in a mystery. Except this time I couldn't put it down. Second, it's creepy, very creepy. And yet, I couldn't put it down.<br /><br />You know from the book description that two teens, Zipp--unemployed, not terribly bright, but sort of decent--and Andreas--attractive &amp; charming, with an expectation that things will go his way--who are going not much of any where in life, liven up their evening by steeling a woman's handbag out of her baby stroller. Things do not go as planned, of course; the stroller rolls away toward a cliff over the sea Zipp tries to run for it, but realized he can't catch it and the boys take off. Still short of beer money, Andreas comes up with plan B. They follow an old woman to her home, where Andreas will get inside &amp; rob her while Zipp waits outside. The time, things REALLY don't go as planned. Andreas doesn't come out. <br /><br />There really are no particularly likable characters here, except perhaps for the inspector, who actually is more of a minor character than usual. <br /><br />This puts me in mind of Stephen King's "Misery" in terms of some of the psychological mess enveloping key characters. And that's all I'm really going to say, for fear of spoiling it for you.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3165269892" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3165269892?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denise Mullins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denise Mullins" href="/user/show/34599955-denise-mullins">Denise Mullins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3165269892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6949022633014987545">Andreas and Zip, two teen miscreants, go on a night of wilding resulting in various degrees of tragedy and chaos until they stumble upon an elderly woman who irrevocably turns the tables. There can be little sympathy evoked for the miserable duo, due to Karin Fossum's vividly visceral characterizations, which are disturbing in themselves.<br/>Admittedly, the jarring narrative which often shifts point of view from paragraph to paragraph may be too much for some readers to tolerate. However, this adds </span>
  <span id="freeText6949022633014987545" style="display:none">Andreas and Zip, two teen miscreants, go on a night of wilding resulting in various degrees of tragedy and chaos until they stumble upon an elderly woman who irrevocably turns the tables. There can be little sympathy evoked for the miserable duo, due to Karin Fossum's vividly visceral characterizations, which are disturbing in themselves.<br />Admittedly, the jarring narrative which often shifts point of view from paragraph to paragraph may be too much for some readers to tolerate. However, this adds to the intensity and psychological dynamics of the plot which moves at lightning speed.<br />As is typical of the series, Conrad Sejer and his assistant are secondary to the development of the story, but by refocusing on the teens and Irma, a complex web of anxiety is created and sustained.<br /><br />Of the books in the series which I've read so far, this is clearly the most horrific and disconcerting. True to form, Fossum does not relinquish her signature ironic concluding twist. Although this adds to the reading experience, and while it is not one that can be termed “enjoyable”, it is definitely memorable.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6949022633014987545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2923755079" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Steve Payne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/86771367-steve-payne"><img alt="Steve Payne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539009480p2/86771367.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve Payne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve Payne" href="/user/show/86771367-steve-payne">Steve Payne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86771367-steve-payne?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86771367-steve-payne?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86771367-steve-payne?shelf=nordic-noir">nordic-noir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2923755079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12076287401033742075">Two teenage boys rob a new mother, then an older confused woman - but...<br/><br/>Another very good read from Fossum, in this, the fourth book in her Detective Sejer series. It's the getting into the mind of a character that I always love with Fossum's books, and here, being that the character is a confused and frightened older woman, she is often prone to rantings and ravings. There are echoes of this in her later book 'The Whisperer.'<br/><br/>As with many of the books in this series, and unlike many other author</span>
  <span id="freeText12076287401033742075" style="display:none">Two teenage boys rob a new mother, then an older confused woman - but...<br /><br />Another very good read from Fossum, in this, the fourth book in her Detective Sejer series. It's the getting into the mind of a character that I always love with Fossum's books, and here, being that the character is a confused and frightened older woman, she is often prone to rantings and ravings. There are echoes of this in her later book 'The Whisperer.'<br /><br />As with many of the books in this series, and unlike many other authors, Fossum is quite happy to give her detective a back seat and just let things ride. Fossum is different and I can't recommend her books highly enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12076287401033742075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10006469725043380956" style="display:none">When the Devil Holds the Candle is an entry in the Detective Sejur series set in Norway. This book is more psychological thriller than police investigation as much of our time is spent with intricately drawn characters who have slid over the line from good to evil. One of the cover blurbs of the edition I read compares this book to Ruth Rendall's writing. I heartily agree, if you like Rendall this novel should appeal to you. Both writers were able to dig under the public facade of characters to reveal what they kept hidden. </span>

<div id="review_1998286028" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1998286028" />
    <a title="Rachel Hall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28372189-rachel-hall"><img alt="Rachel Hall" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495961295p2/28372189.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1998286028?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Hall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Hall" href="/user/show/28372189-rachel-hall">Rachel Hall</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099565482" href="/book/show/13156157-when-the-devil-holds-the-candle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1998286028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6708926353462129089">As a devotee to Chief Inspector Konrad Sejer and a sucker for the marginalised outsiders who proliferate the novels of Karin Fossum, this book had my name written all over it! When the Devil Holds the Candle is the third outing to be translated into English featuring the combination of compassionate Konrad Sejer and his eager and intuitive sidekick, Jacob Skarre. Although this case takes a good few chapters to unravel and its direction to become clear, it swiftly builds into an compelling invest</span>
  <span id="freeText6708926353462129089" style="display:none">As a devotee to Chief Inspector Konrad Sejer and a sucker for the marginalised outsiders who proliferate the novels of Karin Fossum, this book had my name written all over it! When the Devil Holds the Candle is the third outing to be translated into English featuring the combination of compassionate Konrad Sejer and his eager and intuitive sidekick, Jacob Skarre. Although this case takes a good few chapters to unravel and its direction to become clear, it swiftly builds into an compelling investigation that tests even the imperturbable Konrad Sejer to the very limit. <br /><br />Opening with Skarre encountering an elderly lady who seems possessed and rambles incoherently about a missing person, he is left with the distinct impression that he is dealing with a senile woman lamenting on her husbands impending death. As she flees the station without giving further details she remains on his mind. It is only days later that Skarre is able to make some sense of her words and deduce the true significance of her testimony. From that point on Fossum takes her readers back to the prior days and introduces best friends and errant young men in the shape of good looking and dominant Andreas and his hanger-on and lackey, Sivert Skorpe, better known as Zipp. Although Andreas has a job at the local cash and carry that supplies beer money for the pair it is Zipp who has the car and together they terrorise the town looking for action, creating mayhem and frequently watching action movies. What begins as a simple theft of the purse of a young mother backfires somewhat when she loses control of her pram and her child falls onto the path. Things soon escalates into something seemingly far more serious as Andreas and Zipp seek to rid themselves of this memory and opt for an easier victim. Typically cowardly their next mark is sixty-year-old Irma Funder, a bitter and lonely elderly lady who rails against the obligations and duties imposed by a society where she has never known freedom or been loved. Irma has one friend, but in common with her sterile view of life she considers her merely as someone to spend time with without too much discomfort. As a confident Andreas breaks into her home his failure to re-emerge leaves Zipp with a dilemma; namely how is he to tackle the situation without revealing their criminal intent? As the days pass and the disappearance sends his mother, Runi, to the police, all the while a seriously injured Andreas is lying within the confines of Irma Funder's home. But as the hours turn into days, Irma gives her victim water and eventually finds a purpose in her capacity to condemn reprobate Andreas to either life or death.<br /><br />Once again Fossum delivers a tale of complicated and unhappy individuals and shows the destructive and often unintentional effects when their paths cross. Cleverly Fossum leaves her readers to decide on whether justice is served for any of the involved parties. When The Devil Holds a Candle may leave a bitter aftertaste but is is a powerful analysis of compounding mistakes damning the fates of Fossum's well deployed characters. On a personal note, Sejer's relationship with psychologist, Sara, who he met in the previous case is still in progress, despite his first qualms over their long-term compatibility and in another investigation, that of drunk student Robert charged with murdering his girlfriend, the outcome weighs heavily on Sejer. At times difficult to read yet always providing food for thought and an intelligent commentary on modern society, Fossum proves herself worthy of comparison to the esteemed Ruth Rendell.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6708926353462129089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_134129528" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134129528" />
    <a title="El" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4580171-el"><img alt="El" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1290784909p2/4580171.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134129528?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="El" class="user" itemprop="url" name="El" href="/user/show/4580171-el">El</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4580171-el?shelf=mystery-thrillers-read">mystery-thrillers-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer134129528&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134129528" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4344910201028359469">This is a psychological mystery as well as a police procedural. Unlike PD James' characters (isn't she the "queen" of psychological mysteries?), however, who are often anchored to a single workplace or estate, Fossum's characters roam about and in this book range from middle-aged matron to slacker teenagers. <br/><br/>The miscreants in the book all have deep-seated emotional issues that cause them to do what they do - shame, deception, repression, assumed invisibility that gnaws away at them and causes th</span>
  <span id="freeText4344910201028359469" style="display:none">This is a psychological mystery as well as a police procedural. Unlike PD James' characters (isn't she the "queen" of psychological mysteries?), however, who are often anchored to a single workplace or estate, Fossum's characters roam about and in this book range from middle-aged matron to slacker teenagers. <br /><br />The miscreants in the book all have deep-seated emotional issues that cause them to do what they do - shame, deception, repression, assumed invisibility that gnaws away at them and causes them to want to hurt other people. <br /><br />I liked Inspector Sejer. He isn't the usual strung out (see Rebus, DS Logan Macrae)detective - instead, if any thing, he's a middle-aged man starting a hopeful new chapter of his life, as well as being a dogged investigator. He's very even-keeled and sensible. <br /><br />That said, this isn't really a whodunit as we follow the perpetrators (yes, more than one) through almost everything they do. The book's enjoyment comes from watching Sejer trying to make sense of what's been done and in the many moments of suspense (notice earlier I'd said that we get to see almost everything the perpetrators do; sometimes Fossum stops the scene at a moment of decision, for example). <br /><br />As I'm also one who likes to travel when she reads, I also enjoyed being transported to Norway, if during winter bleakness and to some mundane and grubby spots. The one flaw for me - the ending. I would have liked something stronger.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4344910201028359469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_305298213" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/305298213" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3915017-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437695117p2/3915017.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/305298213?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/3915017-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

          added it



          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of classic Scandinavian crime books</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3915017-anna?shelf=bookcrossing">bookcrossing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3915017-anna?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer305298213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4675834290787913880">Third book in the Sejer series but the first one I read.<br/>Fossum's style (at least in this book) reminds me of some of the other Scandinavian a generation ago crime authors like Sjöwall-Wahlöö and Joensuu. <br/>(Or perhaps it was also influenced by such things as Columbo series in the TV, or vice versa?)<br/>First we follow two young thugs who snatch a purse, and at some point of the thugs disappears. Sejer and Skarre end up turning the town upside down to find out where the thug is and what happened. Less </span>
  <span id="freeText4675834290787913880" style="display:none">Third book in the Sejer series but the first one I read.<br />Fossum's style (at least in this book) reminds me of some of the other Scandinavian a generation ago crime authors like Sjöwall-Wahlöö and Joensuu. <br />(Or perhaps it was also influenced by such things as Columbo series in the TV, or vice versa?)<br />First we follow two young thugs who snatch a purse, and at some point of the thugs disappears. Sejer and Skarre end up turning the town upside down to find out where the thug is and what happened. Less of a mystery and more of a character study with blurred lines between the good and the bad (and the ugly). Or a crime story with Columbo pattern, but without that much investigation as Columbo did? <br />Pretty good in the category of Sjöwall-Wahlöö-Joensuu etc, but I like the stories with a billion twists and turns in them, even if I know who killed whom and why. Actually better than most Sjöwall-Wahlöö and Joensuu I can remember, but still - I want to find some more Nesbø type authors out there. Maybe they should find a name for this type of "cozy kind of procedurals, the old-fashioned Columbo-era Sjöwall-Wahlööish crime book". I'll try some of the other Sejer mysteries when I'll find them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4675834290787913880" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_850116800" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/850116800" />
    <a title="donna_ehm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17628565-donna-ehm"><img alt="donna_ehm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361498784p2/17628565.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/850116800?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="donna_ehm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="donna_ehm" href="/user/show/17628565-donna-ehm">donna_ehm</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer850116800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2122592581945360026">It's a sign of good writing when the main character in your series - a cop, no less - only appears a few times in a book but yet you still find it engrossing. In fact, it's Sejer's colleague, Jacob Skarre, who does more of the heavy lifting in the detecting and investigating departments than Sejer (who admittedly has his hands full navigating a new relationship with a rather feisty younger woman, so we can forgive him if he spends a chunk of time off-screen). <br/><br/>The story is basically from the pers</span>
  <span id="freeText2122592581945360026" style="display:none">It's a sign of good writing when the main character in your series - a cop, no less - only appears a few times in a book but yet you still find it engrossing. In fact, it's Sejer's colleague, Jacob Skarre, who does more of the heavy lifting in the detecting and investigating departments than Sejer (who admittedly has his hands full navigating a new relationship with a rather feisty younger woman, so we can forgive him if he spends a chunk of time off-screen). <br /><br />The story is basically from the perspective of an older woman, who Skarre realizes too late is involved with the disappearance of another character. Her story, her state of mind, her place in society, how she views herself - it's all rather fascinating, but then again, that's a strength of Fossum's writing: her examination of how people are in the world, how they function, why they are who they are, the forces that work for and against them, and how they change in response to them. Another commentator said this was a book about people in need and I completely agree. It's certainly much more of a psychological study than a traditional murder mystery, one that I enjoyed reading. The little twist at the very end - that ties into something the woman said right at the beginning - was nicely done.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2122592581945360026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_769433330" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/769433330" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/769433330?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published">traditionally-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=she-says">she-says</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer769433330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6082551410288274751">This book is the third book in the Inspector Sejer mystery series. This book is much spookier and creepier than the previous two. It also differs from the previous two in that you know who the murderer is from the beginning. A young man goes missing. Where could he be? Is he alive or dead? Fossum is a brilliant writer and makes you think deeply about insanity, and the strange things that happen in life. Her characters live and breathe. I love how she has many different people and stories that al</span>
  <span id="freeText6082551410288274751" style="display:none">This book is the third book in the Inspector Sejer mystery series. This book is much spookier and creepier than the previous two. It also differs from the previous two in that you know who the murderer is from the beginning. A young man goes missing. Where could he be? Is he alive or dead? Fossum is a brilliant writer and makes you think deeply about insanity, and the strange things that happen in life. Her characters live and breathe. I love how she has many different people and stories that all come together brilliantly, slowly, to form a colorful tapestry. I can't wait to read her next book. I highly recommend this book. Translated into English from Norwegian. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6082551410288274751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vySIIqk/U/ErCTR68N9LvODUOHQU+OWI5tLjC/IvRitJmMauk/cVdYWTc9eZT3prFhVeDWIHdvPWP+9arkDZDA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HteoKONP2XL9FXorR5lNEeW6mV1AbJfOFqpi0Wy2Lhnoa+ak2Yef9lOPPYYuCXzGE3v/JDaTBLUmR26AMNmxPg==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7688847984222809778">Karin Fossum (née Mathisen) is a Norwegian author of crime fiction,often known there as the "Norwegian queen of crime". She lives in Oslo. Fossum was initially a poet, with her first collection published in 1974 when she was just 20. It won the Tarjei Vesaas' Debutant Prize. She is the author of the internationally successful Inspector Konrad Sejer series of crime novels, which have been translate</span>
  <span id="freeText7688847984222809778" style="display:none">Karin Fossum (née Mathisen) is a Norwegian author of crime fiction,often known there as the "Norwegian queen of crime". She lives in Oslo. Fossum was initially a poet, with her first collection published in 1974 when she was just 20. It won the Tarjei Vesaas' Debutant Prize. She is the author of the internationally successful Inspector Konrad Sejer series of crime novels, which have been translated into over 16 languages. She won the Glass key award for her novel "Don't Look Back", which also won the Riverton Prize, and she was shortlisted for the Crime Writers' Association Gold Dagger in 2005 for "Calling Out For You".<br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/51610-inspector-konrad-sejer" rel="nofollow noopener">Inspector Konrad Sejer</a></span>
